to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路徑 , 丹佛布萊特和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區域 」 的社區 , 和受害者住在tedxc的年齡 。 他分享了9個常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 讓它們傳播到100歲 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、生物、生物、生物、生物、文化、文化、文化、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹佛•佛特:如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個叫做丹麥雙胞胎的研究顯示 , 只有百分之十的平均人的生活 , 在某些生物限制中 , 被我們的基因分歧 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另一種90%是由我們的生命型態的分歧 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的前提:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個已久的公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人的平均壽命的最佳公式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生奧茲告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 真正的幫助我們活得更久 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松或做yoga ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉 , 或你應該吃湯匙嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當它來到供應時 , 你應該帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙或反反抗呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	純粹的玩樂嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神性 ? 以及我們如何社交 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理學合作 , 而國家研究院 , 找到四個人口 , 確認地理的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把專家的團隊帶進去 , 以準確地通過這些人所做的事 , 分解跨越文化歧視 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位這一點 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想在長期來看一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很難活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有5 , 000人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國最快速成長的人口數量 , 很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而編寫 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們為一個叫做 「 成功 」 的程式編寫 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家認為你有孩子的年齡和另一個世代 , 孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	演化的效果完全不適用 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類之間 , 它是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 為了讓它變成100歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生活方式 , 你也必須贏得遺傳量 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 能幫助緩慢、逆轉 , 或甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有99件事情能讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	除非你腦中氧的大腦 , 幾分鐘內 , 大腦細胞會死去 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	在你的膝蓋上 , 毀掉你的卡車 , 卡車永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以標記 。 我們的大腦可以用平原來槍枝 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	錯了太多事情 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數兆個 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年都被轉過來 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉到那裡時 , 就會造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	基本上 , 它建構了指數 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像現在的日子 , 當我們都打敗了album或gmalbums , 我們會複製一份複製 , 讓我們的朋友們複製這些裝置 , 很快的 , 帶著成功的世代聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 我們的細胞也會發生同樣的事 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人在衰老率高於12歲的小孩 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你沒有辦法慢慢老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡做些什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	重點是 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 對女性來說 , 比較多 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 沿著線的某個地方 , 我們在桌上留了大約12年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來 , 我們能得到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大部分年來他們會免費慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為這些失敗的最佳方法是去觀察世界各地的文化 , 人們活到100歲到10倍的人口 , 比我們更大 , 壽命的壽命是多了十年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們在義大利的海岸有125英哩 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 而是在高地 , 一個叫做nuoro建議的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡 , 我們有這個區域 , 男人活得最長的 , 比我們在美國這裡的十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只接觸到一百歲 , 他們用非凡的勝利來做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 十二歲的居住地仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 加油 , 可以打敗一個比他們更年輕的傢伙60歲 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到基督徒的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	實際上是一群被隔離的年齡文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這塊土地非常不穩定 , 大多是牧羊 , 常常發生 , 不穩定的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食大部分都是以植物為基礎的 , 用他們能帶到田地上 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了全部的小麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂 , 由荷蘭的動物製成 , 一類的起士 , 讓起士在歐加三脂肪酸中 , 而不是來自玉米脂肪動物的脂肪酸 , 還有一種類類類型的葡萄糖 , 比世界上任何所謂的酒精還要高 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密我認為他們如何組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最嚴格的元素之一是他們如何治療老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時暫停 。
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 老年人就會得到更多的平等 , 你的智慧越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你去了薩丁尼亞州的酒吧 , 沒有看到運動的標準 , 你看到了月經的中央人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果 , 結果發現 , 不只對你老年老的父母保持距離 , 大約有四到六年的壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩童來說 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 以及較低的疾病率 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊找到了第二個藍色區域 , 大約800英里的東南部 , 在尼古蘭達州南部 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa實際上是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的地點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方 , 人們擁有世界上最長的殘疾壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活了很長一段時間 , 很快就死在睡眠中 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比美國平均的平均壽命還要長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍之多 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	十五歲的殖民和乳癌的死亡率 , 美國大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的第六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經證明了這些數字 , 他們有很強的教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們怎麼辦 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物是基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約8倍的湯匙 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西還要重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的策略 , 來保持過度的策略 , 如你所知 , 美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們從小盤子中吃掉 , 所以他們通常會在每個地點上吃更多的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不用服務家人風格 , 只要你在說話時 , 就會無心地吃 , 他們會在櫃子裡吃食物 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的廣告 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂所發明 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉、帽子 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是個小說 , 這些人在餐前說 , 要提醒他們 , 當他們胃痛時 , 不再吃80% 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它需要一半小時的感覺 , 才能從你的貝兒到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要阻止80% , 它幫助你保持那件事情 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像ardininia , okinawa有幾個社會建設 , 我們能與長壽聯繫在一起 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道 , 孤立是殺死的 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在下降到一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運地出生在okinawa , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你自動有一半的朋友 , 和你穿過生命的人 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 摩托車 」 。 如果你遇到幸運的話 , 你就會期待你會遇到幸運 , 如果事情變得壞 , 孩子會生病、父母死 , 你總是有你背後的人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的摩西 , 這五位女士已經結合了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成年人的人生分成兩次 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常 , 這意味著退休到簡單的椅子 , 或往亞利桑那州扮演高爾夫的角色 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在奈及利亞語言中 , 甚至沒有退休的字 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之 , 有一個字 , 就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	幾乎翻譯 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的原因 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	為了這十二歲的凱特•馬斯特 , 他的ikigai正在帶著這個火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對於這百歲的漁夫而言 , 它持續捕魚 , 每週就有三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化的機構給了我們一個問卷來給這些中央人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們非常有文化的直覺 , 那些提出問題的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們不斷知道為什麼他們早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	在這102歲的老婦女 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾祖父 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101年分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 要抱著一個偉大的國會議員 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回來 , 她說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我的地理學編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區塊 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一陣子 , 我們看著明尼蘇達的禱告 , 實際上有非常高的中亞人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 在七天的冒險家集中在洛馬林達州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	醫師是保守的方法主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五時慶祝他們在星期五的日日日日日日慶祝他們的日子 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	當時有24小時的聖誕節 , 他們稱之為 「
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們追隨了五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們不尋常的長壽 , 相較於說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位先進主義的女人來說 , 他們的壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異在男性當中 , 甚至更為宣佈 , 她們預期的壽命比美國的郡還要長11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這是一項研究 , 追蹤了大約七萬人的研究 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史蒂夫研究 。 我認為它最終可以說明這個藍色區域的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異性戀社群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	這是白色、黑人、猶太人、亞洲 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共同點是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們對大部分的人生都遵循儀式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	慷慨: 「 章魚一 」 、 「 第29 」 、 「 上帝談論樂高和種子 」 、 「 綠色植物 」 、 「 混亂 」 的標準是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在非常嚴肅的情況下採取這個聖誕節 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們有多忙 , 工作的壓力有多強烈 , 孩子需要開車 , 他們停止一切 , 關注上帝、社交網路 , 接著 , 在宗教裡 , 都是大自然的走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量並不是偶爾的 , 電力是每週完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有它很困難 , 沒有錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	進步主義者也傾向於與其他偉大主義者聚在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一位先進主義者的派對 , 你看不見人們打開吉姆•貝姆 , 或推動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談論下一大自然走路 , 擴展接觸 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會影響彼此 , 以深刻且可測量的方式影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 關於whareham 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	wharehareham97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是數百萬美金 , 但當參加者想要6 , 000美金來建立隱私的本質 , 他說: 「 為了我自己做這件事 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出售了水泥 , 並在周圍騷擾 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預測的 , 也許在第四天 , 他終於在手術室裡 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上的傢伙 ; 那個人在做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97年 , 他每個月仍在做20個開放手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	過去103歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末 , 他喜歡把板子放上板子 , 丟在屋頂上 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這兩座城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從白天開始 , 把她的重量開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在她的根廷有色彩1994年的科迪爾維爾維爾 , 她在聖伯納納多•自由公路下 , 她仍然為七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經在19個硬幣進展 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你見過的唯一一個人 , 他的腳踏車在撒哈拉沙漠上 , 沒有陽光的沙漠 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險比起馬爾德里頓的開槍還大 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 。 」 她對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中常見的歧視者是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地把它放到九歲 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經做了兩種藍色區塊 , 由此而來 , 這些常見的偵測器有了事實 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要打開這裡 , 沒有運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了他們的生活 , 這樣他們一直被固定成實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這一百歲的奈瓦婦女在地面上下降 , 他們每天坐在地板上30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直房子 , 下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到商店 , 或教堂或朋友的房子偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何共識 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 去做yard工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想把蛋糕混合起來 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	這樣燃燒的卡路里和跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做意外的實體活動時 , 它是他們享受的事物 。 他們傾向走路 , 唯一能證明認知的衰退 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式建立他們的生活 , 讓他們有權利的爆炸 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每個文化都需要時間轉移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁文學家禱告 。 第七天的演說家禱告 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這個祖先 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你陷入痛苦或壓力時 , 會引發一種稱為 「 內流感反應 」 的現象 , 和阿茲海默症的所有東西有關 , 和心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	每一天你慢慢15分鐘 , 你將這種衝突狀態轉變成更加反射的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有足夠的目的、愛基加 , 例如奇蹟 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們在生活中活躍 , 值得超過七年的壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天喝一點 , 不太難賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 但很多豆子和子子 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來維持過度 , 讓它們從右邊的桌子中消失 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何連結的 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們首先把家人拿來照顧他們的孩子和老父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於屬於信仰基礎的社群 , 這值得四到十四年的壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們是否會出生 , 或對人的權利 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從脆弱的研究中知道 , 如果你的三位最好的朋友 , 有50%的機會 , 你將會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你與不健康的人討厭 , 那會對時間的影響很大 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友的回收概念是實體的活動 , 鼓舞馬克 , 腳踏車或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝一點點 , 但他們吃得太好 , 而且他們很有信任 , 信任和信任 , 這將會有很大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不行 。 世界歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常從一月開始 , 他們通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長期來說 , 在藥丸或其他東西中 , 沒有短暫的修復 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想到 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 可能是你能做最重要的事 , 多年來 , 多年來 , 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會產生電力 ; 一扇窗戶從清晰的轉換到旋轉的角度 ; 一個充滿音樂的水母 , 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡里娜•莫塔塔說:那時候要和它玩 。 摩托帶我們在一個驚人、冷卻材料的旅程中 , 並且建議 , 我們會想知道他們能做些什麼 , 做些什麼 , 去實驗 , 沉迷人和有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有一位朋友 , 他的祖父建造了一台飛行車和洗衣機 , 讓他能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他不能負擔一輛車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有一段時間 , 當我們了解事物如何運作、如何製造 , 這樣我們就能建立並修復它們 , 或是最少的決定要購買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀的第二半期 , 許多的醫生都失敗了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造商社區和開放資源模型將這些知識帶到我們的生活中 , 並且我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 以組成物件組成 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	最重要的部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料 , 像是紙和紡織物 , 以及它們如何製造 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些驚人的、自閉的塑膠 , 能改變形狀 , 繪製電力 , 那些改變顏色的顏色、發光的顏色、發光的顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以 , 受教育的墨水允許我們繪製電路 , 而不是用傳統印刷電路板或電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我握住的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一種觸覺感應器 , 藉由打開這個小燈光 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	受教育的墨水被藝術家所使用 , 但最近的發展指出 , 我們很快就能在雷射印刷機和筆記上使用它 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一座加密的綿羊 , 充滿了無色的光調粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 一般的加密只會在邊緣上發光光 , 整個表面的光明會在我轉向燈光時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中有兩個已知的應用 , 包括內部設計和多種觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	溫度的溫度改變了顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱的盤子上 , 只能讓溫度比雄性更高 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 其中一個原則的應用是 , 在其他東西中 , 嬰兒瓶裡 , 指出內容是很酷的飲用品 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是少數人所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	在幾年內 , 他們會在許多我們每天使用的物品和技術上 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行汽車科幻小說 , 但我們能有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度 , 按鍵板 , 讓它變成轉換的窗戶 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 為何我今天在這裡談論智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇的是 , 事情是如何運作的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解我們的世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的組成並不足夠 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小量子中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用到如何使用它們 , 很少說他們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 他們大部分都存在在貿易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , kirsty男孩 , 我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是我們的網站 , 任何想要加入我們 , 分享實驗、發表資訊、鼓勵別人 , 每當他們能做到時 , 加入資源 , 例如研究論文和其他製造者 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 在智慧材料上 , 自發的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們應該關心有多聰明的材料 , 以及它們所做的是什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們不能形塑我們不了解的事物 , 而我們不明白和使用的結果 , 最終會縮小我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、我們穿的衣服、我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個智慧材料的世界中 , 我們應該知道和了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的 , 創新總是被固定者所燃燒 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 護士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家 , 由山的騎車來改善 , 到半行車、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 物質科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	智力大學的兩位科學家了解到 , 當他們發表了一篇文章 , 以一個簡單的方法來製造效果的墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦布朗•布朗克 , 他從未經歷過化學體驗 , 直到那時 , 讀到這張紙 , 並在他的製造者太空中繁殖了實驗 , 只用無限的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一顆大烤箱 , 他甚至製造了他自己的旅館混合物 , 根據另一位科學家/maker的直覺 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦在網路上發表了他的結果包括他嘗試的所有事情 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬德丹的主要創新形式是採取一個實驗在大學的良好實驗室 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建它 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這份工作 , 其他人可以拿起他剩下的位置 , 甚至更簡單的過程 , 改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想要提到她的專案目標是要強調製造者的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 他們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但他們設計的限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , hannah的方法 , 是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 讓我們不公開的限制 , 藉由教導材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 在漢娜的許多令人印象的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅紙 , 連接到一個mp3的玩家和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院的mcelocohos研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的論文者 , 從簡單的銅板 , 變成發電品和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的信息 , 讓任何人來複製並複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學的最大範圍之一 , 它允許我們創造出便宜和彈性電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的動脈工作 , 她分享了她的發現 , 打開了一系列新的可能性 , 讓兩者都是美好的、創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	創作者有趣的是 , 我們創造出了熱情和好奇心 , 我們不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常從不傳統的角度來解決問題 , 在過程中 , 最終發現了替代方案或更好的方式去做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人的實驗 , 更多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商 , 我們得創造出更好的機會 , 真正服務我們 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得tednelson必須在1970年代初 , 他寫道: 「 你必須了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦只是科學家所關心的主要責任 , 沒有人夢想在家裡有一人 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你現在必須了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 新興科技的先進知識是確保我們未來所說的最佳方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入了玻璃泡泡 , 鎖定門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛 , 儘管我們只能在我們面前看到幾輛車 , 但如果汽車能與他們身邊的位置和動力分享資料 , 用預測模型來計算所有人的安全路線 ?
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•亨利:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能會被避免避免能避免的意外 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對它:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不想思考的一件事 , 但 , 宗教標誌和好運的查爾斯出現在世界各地的廣告板上 , 我們知道它是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	汽車意外是美國年齡十六歲的死亡因素 , 導致死亡和75%的意外對抗毒品或酒精沒有關係 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以確定 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時在高速公路上開車 , 前面的車子 , 我看到的是巴克的燈 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我心想: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我站在公車上 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不是慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停下來 , 死了 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在巴克上滑雪了 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs踢了 , 車子仍然持續下去 , 我知道它不會停止 , 空氣部落 , 車子被安排 , 很幸運的是 , 沒有人被傷害 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子在停止 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變開車的經驗 , 藉由讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是希望你們想想開車的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車 , 閉上門 。 你在玻璃泡泡中 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接理解你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體中 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你對它調查了一部分的道路 , 在其他金屬巨大的巨人身上 , 超人速度很高 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指導你兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 各位的眼睛不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但是人們要求你做類似的事 , 你想做一件事 , 你要做什麼 , 第一件事 , 他們問你怎麼做 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	用你的眼睛從道路上看 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看你在哪裡 , 轉換你的盲點 , 開車走路 , 不用看你在哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人一樣 , 這是要開車的安全方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做個選擇 , 我會在這裡看嗎 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們在路上做一個奇妙的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做些什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺出錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數意外的事件中 , 司機說: 「 我看不見它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但科技現在存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子和彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到三輛車 , 三輛車 , 到右邊 , 左邊 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們就能看見車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到我們面前的車子的速度 , 看看那傢伙的速度 , 或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙走到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算和演算法和預測模式 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 沒有 。 車子 , 不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和穩定的位置 。
they travel down roads .	他們走在路上 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在出版的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於未來的車子將會在哪裡 , 真的很難預測 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使你在車裡和一些摩托車員來了 ! 85英里 , 雷射盤 , 我知道你有這種經驗 , 沒有 「 走出來 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上可能是上半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、20、30英哩後 , 有人看過那個傢伙 , 只要一輛車 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 衣服 , 估計他會持續85英里 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車子會在耳朵上揮舞 , 順便說: 「 五分鐘 , 摩托車 , 看著 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以做出合理的預測 , 關於汽車如何運作 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	那麼 , 我們要如何達成呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 以汽車之間分享我們的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機 , 我有很精確的點子 , 我在哪裡 , 和我在哪裡的速度有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子 , 有點像是 , 並且在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他汽車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有精確的點子 , 有點像是另一輛車的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享這些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	波伯特和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 估計將結合起來 , 甚至在光線交通時 , 汽車共享gpps資料 , 我們將這個研究從電腦模擬和機器人測試的廣告上 , 讓機器人在車上有真正的感測器:鋼鐵相機攝影機、gps、gps , 和兩個高度的發現者結合起來 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也加入了一段很短的溝通廣播電台 , 機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相抵抗時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把更多的機器人加入混合中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的章節時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須精準化 , 這就是預測模式幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預測軌道 , 你不會注意到那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先把這個傢伙看來有點失望 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他在做這件事 , 你知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你知道哪個驅動者必須在路上取得 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做才能做到最好的所有人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子如何摔角 , 「 你需要脫離呢 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二個是駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在手機上 , 或做一些事 , 他們可能不會在急迫中反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做司機模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測駕駛是否向前看 , 向下看 , 看著手機 , 或用咖啡杯 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測出意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪個車位是最好的位置 , 去計算每個人的安全路徑 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術現在存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們所面對的最大問題是我們自己的願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常令人沮喪的點子 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談到其他車子 , 我們會在路上下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看看你的執照數字 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位能考慮一下 , 如果你真的不想在你後面的青少年 , 知道你是勇敢的 , 那你要死掉的停止 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由分享我們的資料 , 我們能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子來參加你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	x獎博士•狄納斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金的夢想 , 透過飛到上層大氣中 , 飛到沒有重量的重量 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短暫的演講、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬•霍金的彼得•迪倫•霍金 , 位於0gggg創作中 , 彼得•霍金 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些知道我有多熱情的人知道我在打開空間前面的熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界上的重力專家 , 重力的體驗是不可思議的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 由基因組組組組組成 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們握住的競爭 , 第二個x獎項 , 在10天內 , 將100個人類基因組序列 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫做基因組的一百個體 , 我們將它定序成一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊特的椅子 , 那個事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見教授霍金 , 他說他的夢想是旅行到太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以把你帶到零中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	地球上唯一能體驗零的方法 , 其實是肢體飛行 , 沒有重量飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一台飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 你沒有重量25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 重兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你再次做一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的重量 , 以美國太空總署訓練他們的太空人多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才能成為採取行動 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛到史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構和一間公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這麼做 , 你要殺了這個人 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有允許 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在肯尼的空間中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場媒體會議 , 我們宣佈我們的意願去做一個零和派對 , 給他25秒 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	假如它真的很順利 , 我們可能會做三種癱瘓症狀 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為何他想去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他對我說 , 對我來說 , 非常動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命是從災難中不斷增加的風險......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為人類的種族沒有未來 , 如果它不會進入太空 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公共利益 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到kenedy太空中心 , 在nasa車內 , 進入零飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人做捐贈 , 我們收入了150萬美元的捐款 , 給孩子的慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedtter 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整個伺服器 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監控他的血液2氧化碳 , 他的心率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們所有東西都在一個緊急情況下 , 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從垃圾桶降落 , 在那裡 , 梭狀會脫離和土地 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我的夥伴lironlichagg , 我小心地讓他變成0g 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 讓他去體驗無重的狀況 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	一開始 , 醫生說了一切都很棒 。 他笑了 , 然後我們說了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以 , 我們做了第二個雙眼鏡 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的把一顆蘋果漂浮在伊斯蘭的牛頓 , 因為哈威爾•霍金教授在布蘭克的劍橋上握著相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 一個第五和六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七歲和八歲 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶中 , 在我們這顆星球的一生中 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這場非凡的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家davidbolinsky現在有3分鐘的動畫 , 顯示在細胞內的忙碌生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、科學、科技、視覺化、視覺化、視覺化、娛樂、娛樂、電影、醫療、醫學、科技、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞動畫一個細胞動畫
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我從稍微不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 自從我長大後 , 真相和美麗的表達 , 在科學領域 , 和美麗 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己的權利 , 但他們兩者都有非常美好的事物 , 讓他們覺得真相和美麗 , 就像科學和數學的理想雙胞胎一樣 , 一個科學家會想約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真實的表達 , 像是很棒的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你能珍惜的東西 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們是獨一無二的 , 有時很有用 , 通常在事實之後 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以推動一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常對不在科學裡的人是相反的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是描述美的方式 , 通常只能取得你了解語言和語言的合成 , 研究真理和美麗的主題 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , e=mc正方形 , 如果你看看宇宙的永續發展 , 那裡有一個人類理想的理念 , 你可以看到生命必須從宇宙中演化出來 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導的醫學插圖師 , 自從我父親教導的動畫和視覺導師 , 我想要找出一個方法 , 幫助人們了解真實和美 , 透過動畫 , 透過圖片 , 透過說故事 , 以說故事來 , 讓人們不必有證據 , 並且可以被教導 , 才能明白 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生常常在環境中聚集在環境中 , 他們學到的是有真相和美感的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是比較 , 而且它被吸引到真實和美麗的位置 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞肝臟的老鼠 , 你把雞放在那裏 , 直到尾巴已經消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生做這件事 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛的羅伯特•路易斯打電話給我 , 幾年前 , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 他問我是否對我的團隊有興趣 , 並且願意真正改變醫療和科學教育如何在哈佛做過 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們開始探索細胞 , 來探索分子和細胞生物學的真相和美 , 讓學生能夠理解更大的圖片 , 讓他們能在這些事實上都能吸引這些事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	細胞的心理圖像很大 , 非常複雜的城市被微型海灘所吸引的城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微生物真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微軟 , 是美國奈米科技學家的靈活性 , 是自主的、強大、精確、精確、精確的裝置 , 是由胺基酸所組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微游生物的力量是如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	他們能發揮細胞如何複製 , 力量我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	他們賦予我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	我們想要做的是 , 要找出如何將這個故事變成一個動畫 , 將是哈佛的生物維護中心 , 這是哈佛的網站 , 為了它的分子和細胞生物學 , 加上所有的訊息 , 除了所有細菌的東西 , 以外 , 讓這些學生能有內在的觀點 , 以外 , 讓這些學生們能夠在他們的腦海中找到 , 並且在他們腦海中發現 , 並且在他們的心中 , 發現 , 他們的心中 , 並且在他們的心中 , 以外表達出自身心中 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 來發現 , 來 , 來 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 來 , 發現 , 來 , 發現 , 來 , 來 , 能夠找到了這些生物的心靈感知知知 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 來 , 來 ,
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們藉由觀察這些分子如何組成 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有一群巨噬體 , 他們正在觸碰捕捉牆的表面 , 它們會從捕捉牆上的細胞中挑起資訊 , 它們會得到這些資訊 , 這些資訊 , 顯示在外面的某些地方 , 可以看到和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊使他們停下來 , 使他們內心化 , 他們需要讓各式各樣的各樣物件 , 讓他們改變他們的形狀 , 並試著從這筆筆記住 , 找出到底發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子運動 , 我們必須和哈佛科學家和資料庫模型合作 , 原子準確的分子模型 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出他們做了什麼 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用一種真相的方式來做這件事 , 它引發了發生了什麼事 , 但不太真相 , 細胞裡的配偶會阻止病毒發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以 , 我要給你們看的是三分鐘的讀者的第一版本 , 我們所製作的這部電影的第一面版本 。 這是一項正在進行的計畫 , 接下來四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看細胞製造這些小步行機器的路徑 , 他們稱之為ksins , 把這些巨大的大型大型的螞蟻挑戰一個對象的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	繼續電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內的力量非常了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器彼此互相互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們把資訊傳給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	他們會造成不同的事在細胞內發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造它在果蠅上需要的零件 , 來自來自細胞核能的資訊 , 由讀取基因的分子來製造 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡 , 不會有這些微小的微生物 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器缺乏的情況下 , 克里斯 , 非常快 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex運送細胞的傢伙 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫凱斯坦 , 他把一堆全新的製造蛋白質帶到細胞裡 , 不論是要到一個胚胎 , 不管是有機 , 不管是要建造東西或修復的東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬件事情在你一百兆個細胞內 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你沒有真正的做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家想這點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們在學習細胞機械的一些東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們想出了一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 我們真的能夠對我們的健康有許多控制力 , 用我們未來的世代來做些什麼 , 以及我們未來的壽命 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這種方法來發現更真實 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這很令人驚訝的是這些細胞 , 這些微型海灘 , 足以察覺到細胞所需的需求 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	他們一起工作 , 讓細胞做該做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 協助我們身體的巨大特質 , 他們永遠無法正確地看到功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝基•布蘭頓計劃一年 , 看到了國家 , 但當憂鬱工作結束時 , 她的營地變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她的經驗 , 成為美國的一家無家可歸 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、故事故事、故事故事、故事、快樂、快樂、生活、生活、個人成長、貧窮、貧窮、社會、社會
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝基•布蘭頓:我是無家可歸的那一年 , 沒有家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個好奇的人 , 所以22年來 , 身為記者 , 我學會如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到了我如何做的事之一 , 就是成為隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為一個無家可歸的無家可歸 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我把工作當作報紙編輯 , 在我父親死了一年二月之後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我很辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事時 , 我有很多想要感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都停下來了 。 我決定 , 一年內生活在一輛車上 , 這樣做就好像一個長的營地旅行一樣 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	我把我的貓包包起來 , 我的旋轉器和我的營火 , 進入1975年的飛行車 , 把車退到陽光上 , 完全無法意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一 , 社會平等生活在永久的結構中 , 甚至是陰影 , 身為一個人有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒意識到別人對現實的負面感知有多快 , 如果我們放下它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在銀行很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地展示 , 我常常吃 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間重新放鬆和悲傷 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱 , 我爸爸的死亡 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須得到全職的工作 , 來支付鈔票 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時的春天轉變成一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	任何地方都不可能公園 , 不用很明顯 , 我和狗有一隻貓 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓在車上穿過一扇開窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	蛋白質在照顧小白天 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	無論如何 , 我都用辦公室大樓的員工 , 卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共餐廳洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度很少降低了80度的水平 , 使得睡眠很難睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中旋轉了 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰的冰塊在幾小時內融化 , 很糟糕 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我不負擔不起要找到公寓 , 或無法負擔負擔的公寓 , 讓我有推特和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們 , 所以我待在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱使我太生病了 , 在我的車外的五十英尺外 , 我用一塊錢和垃圾袋當成廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天天氣設置時 , 溫度降低了 。 他們就在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面臨了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停了不同的地方 , 所以我會避免被警察所注意到 ,
i didn't always succeed .	我不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感受到我人生的控制 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或發生了什麼事 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 成為一名無家可歸的女人 , 住在車裡 , 帶著我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商沒有降落 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才智 , 我的尊嚴 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於我保持的一切 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我更深入深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終有人把我推向無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我走了 , 三天沒有洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和任何人一樣脆弱和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是喝酒 , 或高度 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數位無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 為什麼你在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人都看不見我 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸 , 沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給了我憂鬱症的反應 , 我記得: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 沒多久 , 她聽過那位俄羅斯 , 一個全國的新聞記者 , 一直在談我在國家的t.v 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一本關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在tim的新書中 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做這個演說節目 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , 俄羅斯 , 前面的 「 會議 」 , 談到我的寫作 , 當我住在沃爾瑪停車場時 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 是因為那時候 , 我是作家 , 或者我是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以 , 我在書店裡 , 我找到了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 。 我走了我的命運 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起改變生活 。
and i started writing again .	我再次寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	在接下來的一年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我在贏得獎勵 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再看不見 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人都工作完整工作 , 同時生活在車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續被忽略並犯罪 , 在你的車輛或街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 主要保持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你見過一個 , 參與他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	如果有希望的話 , 人類的精神可以克服任何東西 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是為了無家可歸的女生 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你給你下一名panhandler的錢給你 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不住在哪裡 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或在任何時候的情況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在沃爾瑪停車場裡 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到一種方式 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxche , thailand的 " mr. " schahiviravayaravaya , 帶我們走過國家大膽的計畫 , 到1970年代開始 , 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多frank , 很有趣和非常有效的談談內容 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球性議題、健康、科學、科學界、文化、文化、文化、全球性議題、全球議題、全球性
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	墨西亞維拉瓦亞:mr.保險套如何讓泰國更好的地方做得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 我還是個年輕人 , 國家非常貧窮 , 許多人住在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們沒有從福利計畫或貧窮的計劃開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭平台開始 , 追蹤一個非常成功的女兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:去找孩子 , 到母親 , 然後跟著家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在 , 讓我回到為什麼我們需要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭的七個孩子在3.3%成長 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來準備藥丸 , 我們有非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有作為一個答案 , 我們沒有問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和候選人 , 他們也是女性 , 做了一件很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這真是太棒了 , 但它只佔了百分之二十的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做的事 , 只留給他們說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人士 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 黃色標誌下方 , 我希望他們沒有寫過 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那些日子 , 我們比可樂更大 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選擇的人就是我們選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中被知名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們是很恐怖的 , 他們練習了家庭規劃自己 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應藥和保險套 , 在全國各地的每一個村落 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們去了 。 我們去找那些被視為解決方案的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不管有人 , 你都能看到那些女人的船 , 賣東西是漂浮的市場銷售香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕劑 , 無論你找到人 , 你會在泰國找到避孕性 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裡 , 藍色的 , 不是黃色的黃色 , 讓僧侶發出熱水 , 來為家人的聖水和保險套 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片是全國各地的 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以 , 村莊裡的一些僧侶在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 不想我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它被賦予了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去了老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何能讓人性更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過15萬人被教導家庭規劃的家庭規劃 , 一個新的字母 , 出生 , 為保險套 , 我為伊德 , 創立了大量的基因組 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	接著 , 我們有一個蛇和湖泊遊戲 , 丟掉掉掉掉 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何預期的規劃上降落 , 你會往前移動 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天晚上都會拿藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 向前移動 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了一套保險套 , 非常好 , 叔叔 , 往前移動 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝酒 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再一次 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育、課堂娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套相關的種族 , 我們有孩子的共享冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久以前 , 國會被稱為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對於窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變成一個女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年介紹了第一項微型編輯計畫 , 那些組織的女性說: 「 我們只想把家庭規劃的女性交給女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們跑的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年後 , 它仍在發生 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 而是一個基礎的微型設施 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個很大的組織 , 來操作它 , 由村民們自己運作 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能看不到泰國的男人 , 總是女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不論他們想要幫助或不願幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月第四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供大量的基因組 , 但特別是 , 美國男士到巴西的前方 , 就在他的山大使館的住宅中 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們這個房間 , 讓它非常適當 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	由於它接近午餐的時間 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的煤炭 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你得到兩個品牌 , 可樂和pepsi 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得熱門會更符合象徵 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是這個 , 年輕人稱之為威廉•波爾 , 他為美國大屠殺工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他的主管是半個吃飯 , 他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國製造了很多新聞 , 它也激發了一些人 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 再過來 , 我會做很多人 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	這一切 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是一樣的東西 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定cocola是否遵循我們 , 或者我們遵循cococola , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的案例 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有堅強的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	然後愛滋病來到達泰國 , 我們必須停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的工作並不受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 要求借款300個電台站 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們比政府更有槍 , 比政府更有槍 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們可以幫助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據之後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 你可以用所有的無線電站、電視站 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們去了空氣波 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	接著 , 我們得到了一個新的總理 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 梅西 , 你能加入嗎 ? 」
