so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要重建性和程式化 , 讓它完全被動化 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素完全相同 , 它們都偏見了 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	每個鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想把右或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組合鏈時 , 你基本上是編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你告訴每個單位是否應該轉換或左右 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你打破鏈時 , 它會折疊成你所編寫的任何公式 , 以此為例 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個案例中 , 兩個立方體在彼此旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以編寫任何三維形狀 , 或維度 , 兩個維度在這個鏈上完全被動 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	這告訴我們未來是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為它告訴我們 , 自組裝的新可能性 , 複製 , 在我們的身體結構中 , 我們的建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	由於你有新的能力來計算 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物 , 我們的橋樑 , 機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很棒的平行和分散的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這對此很令人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為這些計畫 , 我剛剛剛展示的只是一個小步驟 , 如果我們將這些新的自我組合的世界實現這些新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們一直到月球 , 我們捕捉了大陸 , 甚至在海洋中最深的地方 。 接下來的世代 , 要探索 ? 生物學家和探險者建議這個答案:幾乎所有東西 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 和不可思議的世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學、科學 , 及生物多樣性 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	納森•沃夫:什麼是剩下的探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近 , 我去拜訪了貝蒂 , 威斯康斯 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮幸一個偉大的二十世紀探險家 , 羅里普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他美國自然歷史博物館時期 , 安德魯引領了一系列的探險 , 來到達加比沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他真的是個數字 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在地上 , 威斯康斯 , 我給了一群中學學生的公開課程 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡告訴各位 , 如果ted的演講比這裡更有害 , 它會試著把一群人的注意力放在一千二十二十五分鐘的教堂上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在課程結束時 , 他們問了一些問題 , 但從那時起 , 我真的很困惑 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們當中有許多人在地球上探索的偉大時代 , 在下一個世代 , 他們必須去外太空 , 或最深的海洋 , 才能找到更明顯的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是如此嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	對我們來說 , 到底沒有什麼重要性 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想我最喜歡的探險家在生物學史上 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這位是聯合國世界的探險家 , 馬丁斯•北吉尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , 北京人開始發現菸草疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中得到感染的果汁 , 他會透過較小的濾器來濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到他所感受到的一點 , 比以前所知的細菌最小的生命形式更小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字給他謎團的名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱它為 「 毒品 」 的病毒拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在未知的病毒中 , 北京人真的為我們打開這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒在地球上製造了大部份的基因資訊 , 比其他生命的基因資訊還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 對於這個世界有著巨大的實用應用 , 像是天花的消滅 , 這種疫苗對抗溫暖癌症 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類的彈性病毒所造成 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	北京發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	一百年前 , 北京發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但是我們意識到我們地球上大部分基因資訊的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們探索未經的世界 , 像是深酷的序列 , 讓我們能做更多 , 不僅僅僅是滑雪表面 , 觀察特定物種的個人基因組 , 看看整個尺寸 , 關於微生物的社區 , 和周圍的社區 , 來記錄這些物種的基因資訊 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技術應用到土壤中 , 到皮膚 , 以及在之間的所有東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們在常規的基礎上 , 找出爆發造成的爆發造成的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	請給你們看一下這怎麼運作 , 想像一下 , 我們每一人拿了一根納西根 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常尋求呼吸病毒的呼吸病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們會看到的第一件事是大量的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因資訊 , 我們會看到許多人的遺傳信息 , 當然 , 許多人的基因資訊 , 還有細菌和病毒資訊 , 從鼻子中完全無害 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常令人驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡的遺傳資訊的百分之二十 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們沒有線索 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們研究這種數據的小組 , 我們當中的一些人已經開始稱之為資訊生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前所見的任何東西 ; 它有點像我們自己的基因資訊中所未見的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你的鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質如果我們看你的腸子 , 到40%或50%的資訊是生物暗物質
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對穩定的血液中 , 大約有百分之二的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法用我們以前所見過的任何東西來配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始 , 我們認為這可能是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深厚的序列工具相對是新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當他們變得更準確 , 我們決定這些資訊是生命的形式 , 至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 只在它們的基礎上 , 有一個非常令人興奮的可能性:在這個基因資訊中埋藏在生命中 , 這些基因信息的特徵是未知生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	正如我們探究生物學的這些弦 , tc和g , 我們可能發現一個完全新的生活 , 例如北京人 , 基本上會改變我們對生物學的本質 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這也許讓我們能辨識出一種癌症的原因 , 來影響我們或辨識出我們不熟悉的爆發來源 , 或是在分子生物學中創造一個新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很榮幸地宣佈 , 和史丹佛和加州大學的同事 , 我們現在正在開始探索生物暗物質 , 探索新的生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百年前 , 人們意識到病毒的形式 , 那些在地球上大部分基因資訊的基因資訊 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能很驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到在我們的鼻子下的新生物 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	事實是 , 我們可能在地球上的所有大陸 , 我們可能發現了外面的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有剩下去探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的善意提供一個重要的教訓給下一代的探險家 , 像那位年輕女孩 , 來自威斯坦 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們說過這一課 , 那就好像這樣:別假設我們現在所認為的一切是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇探索的領域中 , 你選擇去探索的黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周遭都有未知 , 等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	合法的科學家daviddesch把理論物理放到後面 , 來討論更緊急的事:我們物種的生存 。 第一步是解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛診斷在我們的宇宙中 , 大衛診斷在宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要出一個肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這樣做 , 但我想從所有人都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一 , 事實上 , 大部分被記錄記錄的歷史 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或其他環境 , 特別是維持我們的進化或創作 , 如同過去被認為和現況最重要的 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	今日這個想法有一名戲劇性的名字:太空船 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	而這個想法是 , 在太空船外面 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而內部就是我們所依賴的 , 我們所依賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只能得到一個機會:如果我們把我們的太空船混在一起 , 我們就沒辦法去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道 , 對於大部分人類歷史的信念相反 , 人類並不是 , 事實上 , 存在的幽默 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	史蒂芬•霍金說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學雕塑 , 在典型的星球上繞著一個典型的星系 , 也就是典型的星系 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 每個人都知道的兩件事就是說我們在一個很不典型的地方 , 獨特的定位置 , 第二個是說我們在典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你把這兩句深度的真相看待你的生活決定 , 那麼他們似乎和彼此相互衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這不是避免兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 , 典型 。 嗯 , 咱們來看看 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 和化學雕塑 , 完全不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要做幾百英哩的方向 , 再回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆 , 或化學雕塑 , 只要你更進一步看 , 太陽、太陽系等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這還是不典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星出現在星系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中大部分的地方 , 宇宙中的一個典型的地方 , 完全沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	再進一步來說 , 我們在銀河外面 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有著巨大的銀河系 , 在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們從這裡來了十萬個光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但現在我們仍處在宇宙中典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你必須進入一千倍的內在空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的昂貴之中 , ted已經提出了一個高解析度的虛擬實境 , 以內在空間的觀點來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 請看 , 看看嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你看到 , 在內部的太空空間中 , 完全是黑暗、鋼鐵黑暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	很黑暗 , 如果你看近期的星星 , 那顆恆星就變成超新星 , 而你直接盯著它 , 當光接觸到你時 , 你仍然不會看到一個溫室 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙是這麼大又黑暗的 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管是超新星的事實如此明亮 , 最棒的一個事件 , 它會殺死你在幾年的光年內死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從內部空間來看 , 遠離你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	它也很冷 , 比絕對零度還要低三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它非常空氣 。 真空中有一百萬倍的密度 , 目前地球上最高的科技能創造出的最佳科技 。 所以典型的地點是來自這個地方的 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的不典範 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能不能把燈光放回去嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們要如何知道一個遠離的環境 , 如此不同 , 外星人 , 從我們所習慣的任何東西 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球是我們的環境 , 在我們的形式中 , 創造了知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那意味著什麼呢 ? 看看我們剛剛從這裡開始 , 用望遠鏡 , 你會看到像星一樣的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 平方形 」 。 原本的意思是 「 量化物 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著 , 看起來像星星 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是幾十億年前的 , 數十億年前的光年後 , 銀河系的中心的材料會降低到超大量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場引導了一些重力崩潰的能量 。 有些重要性 , 回到了巨大的噴泉的形式 , 我認為它是幾兆陽光 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理 , 幾乎不會像這種噴泉的物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法生存在它之中 。 語言在試圖描述它時 , 語言會突破它會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像是排除超級新星爆炸 , 但在日本的範圍和數百萬年間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射發生在數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學螢幕可以準確描述、模型 , 並預測 , 向上解釋 , 除了你所看到的 , 在現實中發生的事情 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦有精確的運作模式 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是一個超級公平的圖像 , 雖然它也包含了它 , 但一個解釋模型 , 將相同的數學關係和相同的構造 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這種知識是知識的 。 如果那還不夠奇妙 , 一個結構組合了另一種結構 , 會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的成長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體物體 , 不像它們一樣 , 不像它們一樣 , 不管有數學和實際的結構 , 都能再做更多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是化學螢幕是不同的 。 這個化學螢幕有普遍性的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了 , 不斷地增加精準 , 所有東西的結構 。 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是它本身的結構 , 包含在其餘的物理現實中 。 所以 , 目前 , 目前 , 物理物理學的定律 , 還能讓它成為實體世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 如何將這個特殊的關係和宇宙的其他其他的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的明顯 , 我是說 , 這是真的 , 但它是錯的 。 其中一件事是 , 它沒有任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的失調 , 沒有奇蹟 。 沒有奇蹟 。 它只用我們有的三件事 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 需要一個電腦 , 不需要製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體在我們所發現的知識上 , 來記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 更不適當 , 但正如 「 知識 」 、 「 解釋 」 的開放創造 , 是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們在三百年前就開始測試 , 例如 , 牛頓的重力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 我們以前曾經做過的證據在地球上的每一平方公尺上下降 , 數十億年後會持續下降 。 而對其他科學來說也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	儘管我們知道 , 證據證明所有科學的最基本真理 , 就是要在地球上採取 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在內部的空間中 , 這三種正式的設備 , 知識的開放創意是他們最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 它是空的 ; 它很冷 , 那裡是黑暗的 。 還是嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另一個家庭誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像一下 , 在內部空間中有一個立方體 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 位置是人類標準的 , 但這仍然意味著它有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造 , 比如 , 一個自我控制的空間站 , 這裡有一群科學家 , 要創造一個開放的知識 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 科技超越了科技 , 甚至加入了國際空間的氫氣 , 形成其它元素 , 等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個令人難以置信的宇宙中 , 如果物理定律不被物理定律 , 那麼 , 可能如何阻止我們從做這件事 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 知識很重要 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動使用能源供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應器和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再一次 , 它在人類感知上暗暗 , 但你只需要做一座望遠鏡 , 甚至是現今的設計 , 看看 , 你將看到同一個銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	隨著更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些銀河裡 , 你就能做天體物理學 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習原始粒子物理、化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	或許最困難的科學是生物領域的旅程 , 因為它會花上數億年才能抵達最近的生命星球 , 回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 很抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有像生物領域一樣 , 我認為我們可以用一億年的時間來做 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 國際空間確實包含了所有開放知識的設備 。 在宇宙中任何地方 , 任何地方 , 都可能變成我們是一樣的擁抱 , 假如如何在這裡的知識 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是獨特的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果國際空間可以創造一個開放的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 。 所以地球 。 所以 , 這是一個污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很可怕 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種宇宙知識的觀點 , 或許我認為要讓我們感到非常特別 , 但它也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 沒有特定的知識 , 要存活在宇宙中 , 我們不會生存它們 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星才能離開幾年 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁礁最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱的書 , 從天體物理 , 到科學實驗錯了 , 最重要的是 , 和大眾毀滅的武器有關 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會來拯救這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在會議中談到這件事 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為 , 可能性是對的類別 , 來討論這個問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我跟他同意 , 我們能存活下來 , 我們可以無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它不依賴機會 , 但 , 不論我們在何時創造出相關知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並非每次都沒有被忽略 。 物種永遠都會滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終於結束了 。 大部分的物種和所有文明都存在現在都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為這個範圍 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望是用我們物種的特徵 , 我們的文明 , 我們的文明 , 從其他的名字中 , 我們和物理定律的特殊關係 , 創造出新的解釋 , 新知識是存在的 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在 , 讓我應用到目前的爭議 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只是為了說明我所謂的事物 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是對的物理學家 , 在全球暖化的情況下 , 我只是一名layman 。 理性的做法是要嚴肅地使用科學理論 。 根據理論 , 這理論已經太晚了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們現在最好的選項是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 像是肯亞的提案 , 它的限制在經濟活動上 , 或其巨大的成本 , 或任何東西 , 已經被任何合理的測量造成災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	那些倡導的行動甚至沒有意願解決問題的行動 , 要把它放到一點點 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 已經太晚了避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 從任何人意識到危險之前就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	它可能已經太遲了 , 70年代最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放的排放將會預防數十億年齡的新冰層 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	聽起來很明顯 , 我不知道為什麼這不是公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們無法永遠知道 。 當我們知道更大災難時 , 要如何在災難本身的成本中解決它 , 那麼就不會有太多的辯論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防 , 沒有預防原則 , 還能避免我們尚未得到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個問題來解決 , 不僅僅是問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	事實是 , 預防等於一磅的治癒 , 但如果我們知道該預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打開 , 那麼醫學的科學並沒有限制教導你如何避免懲罰 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學停止尋求治癒和專注於預防 , 那就不會達成一點 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界在這個時刻 , 規劃要強迫減少氣體排放量 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計劃來降低溫度 , 用計劃來活在更高的溫度上 , 而不是所有成本 , 而是有效地和便宜 。 有些計畫存在 , 像是在太空中游過的鏡子 , 來反射太陽光 , 鼓勵水產出更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此刻 , 這些東西正在嚇壞研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力面對這個問題的中心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	而我們還沒意識到的問題 , 要把正確的能力放棄 , 而非無限的幸運是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以 , 拿兩塊石頭桌子 , 把它們卡在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 卡維: 「 問題是不穩定的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一輛車子: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它陷入壞規則的系統 , 經濟學家保羅揭露了一個大膽的點子: 「 查爾斯城市 」 , 城市管理了國家聯盟 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治議題、政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅•羅馬的徹底想法:查特城市的城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它對我們來說是非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在上市的街道上做作業 , 因為他們在家裡沒有電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到了像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色襯衫中的一個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	讓我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我會打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這裡是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson能取得可愛的技術 , 像是手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的科技 , 來在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	一個字 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防一種贏家解決方案 , 當人們可以把新技術帶進去 , 讓他們能用到像nelson這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在規則下運作 , 也就是說 , 它必須在非常低、低的價格下賣電 , 事實上 , 一個價格太低 , 它的價格會低於每一塊錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 不是資源 , 也不是獎勵 , 把很多其他使用者都拿出來 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看過 , 可以有不同的規則 , 規則是商業收入小利潤的 , 所以他們有更客戶的獎勵 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這類的規則是nelson公司的手機公司 , 把他的電話從下方的電路來銷售他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則如何運作 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電力的規則 , 但從商業及消費者們想保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被禁止讓他脫離贏家解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson在街頭上研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有些規則是可以改變規則的嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想提出一個普遍的觀點 , 我們能做出實際的觀點 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多選擇 , 在許多國家 , 在許多國家 , 也有更多的選擇 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導者的選擇 , 例如給總統選項來提高電力的價格 , 採取一個選擇 , 讓人們在經濟中想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能夠持續消耗電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一面或另一邊 , 你會有緊張或摩擦 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更有選擇的方式 , 那會給我們一系列的規則 , 來改變陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , nelson也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的損害效應 , 規則可以讓人們在黑暗中留在黑暗中 , 看看地球的nasa的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查亞人 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你把這裡放大 , 你可以看到北韓 , 外線 , 就像一個黑洞和鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會很驚訝地了解北韓的規則 , 讓人們在黑暗中留下來 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 要知道北韓和南韓是很重要的 , 從法律和規定的角度開始的規則 , 但也在了解、規範、文化、價值、信仰的深處 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致他們一組規則的多樣性路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	我們能改變人類的改變 , 可以改變我們用彼此互動的規則 , 更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	在海地上放大 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 和鄰居相比 , dominican共和黨 , 大約有相同的居民數量 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	兩種國家都是黑暗的 , 比起波多黎各的居民 , 只有半數的居民 , 或dominican共和黨 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能是壞事 , 因為政府是弱勢的 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不僅僅是規則是壞的 , 因為政府太強壯又壓迫了 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想用好規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能只花掉 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建造 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅地展示了兩種可能和規則的挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這個圖表的開端 , 中國是世界上的高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先前的科技 , 像鋼鐵、印刷、槍械 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從未採用過 , 至少在那段期間 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵那些想法的擴散 , 可以鼓勵傳播速度 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了原則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界其他地方移到中國 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 身為世界上其他國家創新的國家 , 都在開發新科技 , 同時也開發新規則 , 中國是從那些進步中脫離 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持穩定 , 如同它在世界上其他地方放大了 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一個圖表 , 看看最近的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	中國平均收入的平均收入是美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到 , 大約百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 有些改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國長大了 , 中國開始很快地和美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回去地圖 , 你就可以把線索帶到中國的規則中 , 導致中國規則的戲劇改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地點 , 你可以在線上的邊緣看到 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	蜜蜂kong是一小部分的中國 , 大部分的20世紀 , 在一個非常不同的規則中 , 比其他主要的中國規則 , 由工業市場經濟組成 , 由英國人所組成的 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個地方 , 數百萬人可以從主島開始 , 開始 , 像縫紉、玩具、玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致了非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是領導人的模型 , 像是憂鬱症的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定把所有主要陸地搬到市場模型上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 把焦慮視為對他人而言 , 明白 , 提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其在中國的每個人馬上轉移到市場模式 , 他們被創造出一些特殊的區域 , 以某種程度來說 , 英國的做法:讓機會和市場規則合作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創造了四個特殊的經濟區塊:中國可以來工作 , 城市也很快地長大 , 外國公司可以進來 , 製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個區域有一個叫做snzhen的城市
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有個台灣 , 讓許多人擁有的iphone , 他們用中國的勞工來搬到羊 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特殊區域之後 , 有14個海岸的清潔 , 最後證明了人們可以選擇的成功 , 他們被關在他們所提供的優勢中 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	示範成功 , 導致了整個經濟模式邁向市場模式 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村莊的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村莊太小了 , 只要有數百萬人在好規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變這個國家的規則 , 你不能給大家一個機會 , 看看事情如何發生 , 讓其他人往前嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你這個機會 , 創造新的地方 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	他們足以讓所有我們能在好規則下工作的好處 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是我們認為一個叫做chrter城市的概念 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則中開始 , 要吸引我們需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 去建造基礎建設系統、道路、機場、大樓、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會首先僱用移民的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家人 , 他們會永久地生存 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著那個圖表 , 人們會在那裡移動 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴展這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以再次做一次 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些是被捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們允許在無所居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未被監禁的地位開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以活在新頻道下 , 但沒有人被迫活在它下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	我們需要的最後一件事是領導人的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導人 , 我們需要讓國家之間合作的可能性:國家合作 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式合作 , 共同建立 , 首先是市場模式 , 然後將它擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國不明顯地 , 透過香港的行動 , 來減少世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀的愛滋病計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這些合作夥伴再次複製 , 我們就能在世界各地得到這些益處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及負責任的程度 , 一個國家的控制程度 , 到另一種國家 , 去採取某些負面責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這樣說時 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 。 但重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 這種情緒會出現 , 可以讓我們回想 , 可以把我們的能力縮小 , 我們的興趣在嘗試探索新點子 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義的壞事 , 在我們一些愛滋病計畫中 , 它涉及了合作和欺騙的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模型是關於選擇 , 領導者和領導人 , 和那些能生活在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是合作和欺騙的抗拒 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在練習上演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來看看特定的領導人 , 拉多•卡羅斯特 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	它一定會發生在加州的加州 , 他有機會為中國做些什麼 , 但他沒有在古巴島的香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他在南方有一點光 , 那裡有非常特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	這裡有一塊區域 , 包括保安亞摩灣 , 一個治療給美國政府的責任 , 對於曼哈頓大小的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	加拿大總理說: 「 看 , yankees有一個糟糕的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的管理區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新城市可以在那裡建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	咱們來到附近 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回來 , 但這將會是將將現代經濟和現代世界連結起來的門道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 其他的模型可能在哪裡 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領袖談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到特殊區域的概念 , 人們可以把原則當作規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	創造新的規則 , 讓人們不同心協力 , 以及同心協力的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全知道 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 讓長期投資者能夠建立運動 , 建立道路 , 在新城市中 , 他們能做出更可信的承諾 , 如果他們和一個夥伴合作 , 就能做出更有信心的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在某些排列中 , 有點像是一群人的帳戶 , 你把土地放在明天的帳戶和另一半國家的責任 , 要為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地 , 可以建造新的城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在沿岸飛行的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這塊土地 , 有數十億人可以活下來 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們一般化 , 想想不單單單單一或兩個圖表 , 但有數十億個城市 , 可以為數十億人創造地方 , 或許有數十億人會搬到未來的城市 , 那裡有足夠的土地 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	世界各地 , 如果我們在夜間看光 , 其中一件錯誤的事情就是 , 視覺上 , 它看起來是世界上大部分的建築已經被建造出來的 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我向各位展示為什麼這錯了 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這個代表所有土地 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	將它轉化為地球上所有可行的土地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人居住的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到其他方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有三十億個都市居住在地球上只有3%的阿拉伯土地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們會像這樣做 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從三分之三的阿拉伯土地 , 到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅減少地球上人類足跡 , 透過建造更多的城市 , 來建造更多人可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是好規則的 , 他們可以成為人們安全的城市 , 來自疾病和不公平的危機 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們可以得到像電力一樣基本的營運 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	那麼 , 要怎麼做才能開始建造第一個查爾斯城市 , 把這個規模擴大 , 來建造更多呢 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助有手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的事是寫出一些細節 , 寫在這個手冊上 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不想讓我們經營城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放棄學術 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們思考像這樣的問題 , 假設它不僅僅是加拿大 , 還能處理raulcastro的處理 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 和西班牙 , 可能是古巴想要成為四公路的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們該怎麼寫治療呢 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這種情況比較沒有預期 , 但很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何改善這一點 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時所擁有的土地的價值 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭 , 但學校系統和健康照護系統 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 後來 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們協助建構這個區塊 , 建立基本規則 , 以正確的方向 ,
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有許多其他細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓大樓低成本和可負擔的成本 , 以第一份工作的人 , 組成像iphone , 但讓這些建築能有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以他們不在地震或颶風下降落 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節可以成功 , 但是我們已經開始追求這些事情的人已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有想像力 , 除了失敗 , 這將會讓我們從真正的全球贏家解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我結論一下這張照片 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	因爲我們能如此消失 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享點子 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不是很害怕的物體 , 在那裡 , 分享意味著我們每次都少了 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們就會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們這樣思考思想時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:我們如何與彼此互動的規則 , 例如 , 我們有一個稅制系統 , 支持一個研究大學 , 讓某些知識免費 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們有一個系統 , 在政府辦公室中 , 我們有自己的土地 , 人們可以被視為是冷凍 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是為了改變規則的規則而創新 , 所以我們不用不好的規則 , 那麼我們可以繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 , 所以像nelson和他的朋友不需要在街道下研究更久 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學的先驅驅驅從他的前境中突破 , 來談談數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 發現了海洋多樣性的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物學、創業家、遺傳學、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技
craig venter on dna and the sea	在dna和海上 , craig發射器 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	在突破時 , 我被幾個人問我關於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀主義者很明顯是極端的 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內我要告訴各位 , 我們要如何從讀基因密碼轉換到第一階段 , 開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	只有10年前 , 我們出版了第一代自由有機體的第一序列 , 海氣流感染 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這計畫從13年下降到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八個小時的基因組做同樣的實驗 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組已經增加了:大部分人類的病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	大約十年前 , 基因組在這個階段裡 , 在今年結束時 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 , 它在數百年的秩序上 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從goordon和貝爾摩爾基金會得到的獎勵 , 到今年的130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的一方項目 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	閱讀基因密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 正如我們所看到的 , 我們在地球上幾乎幾乎沒有用到的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人都不知道 , 因為它們是隱形的 , 但微生物組成了大約一半的生物量 , 所有動物只能製造出大約一分之一的生物量 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是在牛津的人們不常做的事 , 但如果你把它帶到海裡 , 你就會吞下一口海水 , 保持每毫米的細菌 , 大約有一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到兩萬五千種微生物物種被分類為兩年前 , 所以我們決定做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了無害的伊斯蘭探險 , 如同我們所處的偉大的海洋領域 , 嘗試每兩百英里的海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從bermuda開始 , 然後搬到哈里克斯 , 去加勒比海岸 , 加勒比海 , 保羅馬 , 穿越太平洋 , 我們正處於印度洋的過程 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	非常艱難 , 我們正在做這件事 , 其中一部分是幫助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只拿海水 , 過濾它 , 我們收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們的實驗室 , 每24小時的基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	有了這一點 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 視覺化的顏料在我們的眼睛中只有一到兩種生物在環境中有相同的顏色 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上最高的海洋中所有物種都有相同的攝影器 , 用陽光來源 , 作為它們的能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一個海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這個延伸到空氣上 , 和浮游基金會的巨大延伸出來 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或閉上聲音 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們過濾了一些簡單的地點 ; 我們收集了十億個微生物 , 每天在紐約市的建築物上濾出來 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於目前的定序過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在資料集中 , 只要我們透過加拿大 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 我們在海洋中的樣本中看到了巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些有邏輯的感覺 , 以不同的溫度來看 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星攝影 , 根據紅色的溫度 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人驚訝的事情是這些攝影器偵測出不同的光長度 , 我們可以預測 , 根據他們的胺基酸序列 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些從區域到區域的巨大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外 , 在深海中 , 大部分是藍色的 , 攝影師通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當很多的染色體周圍出現時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但他們甚至會再移動到紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了試著找出我們基因複製的評估 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包含我們所有的資料 , 從前進 , 代表地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 大約有2億9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放進基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們剛發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 或是我們發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但是我們在環境中採取的每一種新樣本 , 加上這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於最早發現基本基因、零件和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們觀察所謂的演化樹 , 我們和動物的右上角 ,
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約兩千九百萬個基因 , 我們只有兩萬四千個基因 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物聚在一起 , 我們可能有不到三萬個 , 也許有數十萬個基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在一個慷慨的觀點 , 也許回到理查•達金斯的點子 , 比基因組的角度來說 , 這些基因組成的不同建設 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年間 , dna定序已經改變了dna序列的速度 , 兩次 , 變得非常快速 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組在1995年序列第二個基因組 , 從微生物生殖器開始 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤會說: 「 我心愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	哈姆斯有1 , 800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一半 , 另一個500種基因會比較小的基因 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做交通突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯器只是一小塊dna , 隨機地在基因密碼上隨機的定位 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們在基因中定位 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們製作了所有可以採取翻譯器的基因圖 , 我們稱之為 「 目的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 而你只能定義一個必要的基因 , 基於環境中的任何原始基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用一個更直接的智能方法來處理13個相關有機體的基因組 , 我們試著比較所有這些 , 看看它們的共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些驚人的圓圈 , 我們發現 , 只有173個基因在所有13個生物身上 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	警察擴展了一點 , 如果我們忽略了一個吸引寄生蟲 , 它會擴展更多 , 甚至在310年的核心基因 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 依據你的觀點來看 , 大約有300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	為了證明這些想法的唯一方法就是建立一個人工的染色體 , 用這些基因來建構 , 我們必須在一些基礎的時尚上做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片的dna中合成是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆•史密斯和clythuchison , 我的同事在這個過程中 , 開發了一個令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們合成一個5000多巴士的維爾病毒 , 只有2威脅 , 只有百分之百的準確 , 在其序列和生物學上 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個很令人興奮的實驗當我們剛剛拿到細菌的合成dna注射 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒 , 只有一年前的小兒麻痺病毒 , 但只有十分之一的活躍 , 花了三年才能做到 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個例子 , 軟體現在建立了自己的硬體 , 那就是我們有生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到生物戰場的情況下 , 我最近在參議院委員會之前 , 一個特別的委員會 , 美國政府開始審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 保持現實的重要性 , 和人們的想像力有關 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今所有被定序的病毒都可以被製成 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上對伊波拉或天花很驚訝 , 但這個有機體的dna不是感染的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做出了天花基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正關心的是設計師的病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 試圖創造生物戰略機構 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這個研究真的不穩定 , 該有一點活動 , 才能在未來製造設計師的病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內可能 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是uktic細胞 , 我們有的這些細胞 , 在十年內 , 可能是可能的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以現在我們現在做了數十個不同的建設 , 因為我們可以把這些洞穴和基因放進這個人工染色體中 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把所有人放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一套共通的組合系統 , 將這些元素組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是來自有機體、丹麥無線電廠 , 可以使用三百萬個輻射 , 而不是被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它將基因組組成大約12到24小時後 , 在它的染色體分離之後 , 會分離 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上 , 可能存在於外太空 , 是因為我們的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一杯玻璃噴射器 , 大約有50萬個輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 當微生物坐在底部時 , 就會變得更快樂 , 更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張圖片:這張圖表上方顯示了1.7百萬個輻射的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體分開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	相同的dna自動組成24小時後 ,
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這真的令人驚訝 , 這些生物可以做到 , 我們可能有數千個 , 如果這星球上有數萬種不同的物種 , 可以做到 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是把它們移植成一個細胞 , 沒有基因組 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有很大的潛力 , 不僅能了解生物學的基礎 , 也希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 從我們定序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷酸鹽 , 它在沸水溫度中活著 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 所有的碳都來自環境中 , 它的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的有機體在二氧化碳中存活 , 可捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 不是用石油來做合成過程 , 而是使用碳的機率 , 將它從大氣中取回 , 轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物可以從二氧化碳中生存 , 我們用它來分解水 , 來產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有數個路徑可以被工程化甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	塵埃有一個主要的計畫 , 用挪威的石油來捕捉並將氣體的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短短的一段時間內 , 我想有新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組 」 , 因為這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因組組組成 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天製造一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學 , 透過螢幕進行篩選 , 不論你正在篩選氫生產 , 或化學生產 , 或可能性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	為了了解這些基因的角色 , 會很好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著將光合作用直接從陽光產生氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是氧氣 , 我們有氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為它會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也組合細胞的酵素 , 把複雜的糖分解成簡單的糖和肥料 , 在同一個細胞中 , 來生產乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥廠已經用微生物來進行重大實驗室 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中化合物的化學物質 , 比我們最好的化學學家能產生的更複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環保的回收 , 也許要取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我和倫理和政策研究結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年開始了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 我們應該試著做一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與了這個 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這是個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為許多宗教領袖在使用法律書本 , 他們無法找到任何東西 , 所以 , 唯一的關注是生物戰略的面向 , 但給了我們先前進行這些實驗 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前 , sloan基金會基金會基金剛基金會在這個研究上 , 來找出社會的風險和利益 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 例如我自己應該在這個地區使用 , 我們正在嘗試建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 我們能設計出能製造乾淨能源 , 也許革命發展中國家能做些什麼 , 並透過各種簡單的過程來提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•辛布歐說幸福和成功在我們大多數人的特徵中被根除:我們對過去、現在和未來的方式 。 他建議我們將我們在一步推廣出去改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、思想、心理學、科學、科學、科學、科學、知識、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo是健康的 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和各位分享一些關於時間的秘密力量 , 在很短的時間裡 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始開頭 。 三十秒鐘的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	重點是時間 。 最後 , 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	十、九、八、七、五、四、二、二......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	philipzimardo:我們來到亞當的誘惑的談話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來到亞當 , 不要太願望 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一個 , adam , 不要放棄eve 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想去麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好了 , 再一點 。 什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 , 重點是關於消失、抗拒 , 是的 , 沒錯 , 沒錯 , 反射、反射、現在的焦點和未來 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的虛擬失敗了現在的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年的女孩 , 被性侵和惡性侵害 , 直到婚姻──謝謝你──布希大部份 , 60% , 在一年內被性誘惑給性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都這麼做 , 不用出生的控制 。
so much for promises .	為了承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	咱們來嘗試四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆馬爾瑪球 。 但如果他們等到實驗者回來 , 他們就有兩個 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 要付錢 , 如果你喜歡馬拉夫 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	結果是三分之二的孩子給誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	當然 , 他們無法等待 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒了誘惑 , 後來他們就把現在放棄了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	威爾特•米克爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 回到14年後 , 試圖發現那些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 有巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒了250點的孩子們 , 坐在桌子上升 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這是很大的 。 這就像一組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有太多麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信和決心的 , 對我來說 , 對你來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是未來的折磨而非正式的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個人的研究 , 我們所有人 , 分析你的人類體驗 , 或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	你自動地做 , 不意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化和國家之間 , 在社會階級之間 , 在教育層面之間 , 會在不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們可以被偏見 , 因為你學會去克服一些人 , 並且在別人身上 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做出的決策是什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 你要打擊行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你所感受到的 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱之為 「 文件 」 , 因為他們焦點現在就是這樣 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現代並不重要 。
