it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	一直在於 「 我過去經歷過的情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們將稱之為 「 過去 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在的 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在預期後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來 」 。 他們的焦點在什麼樣子上 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說 , 時間觀點的矛盾 , 是你做出的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 你有一個偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個人 , 有兩種方式可以呈現 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被遺忘 , 兩種方式來成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在過去 , 或被負擔 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可能是現代化的 , 叫做你專注於生命的喜悅 , 或現代主義者 , 不重要 , 你的生活是被控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可能是未來的、設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是透明的未來:命名是 , 生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理的靈活性 , 轉變時間觀點的觀點 , 仰賴這個情況的需求 , 那就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	在過去的情況下 , 現代的未來很高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代的治療方式 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於過去的負面和禮物主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時混合物是你從過去的背景中得到的樣子 。 你將你的家人、身份、你的自我連結 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來所得到的 , 是要穿到新目的 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在得到的 , 就是能源 , 去探索自己、地方、人、人 , 感官 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	例外的觀點比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來的犧牲是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭的時間 。 他們犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲時間 , 犧牲個人的無情 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了同性戀 , 她們犧牲睡眠 , 所以它會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們生活在工作、成就和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted的人共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我長大 , 在南布朗克斯皮托 , 一位醫師家人都住在過去和現場 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 身為未來的一個人 , 他們都做這些犧牲 , 因為老師被介入 , 讓我未來 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我 , 不吃馬拉夫 , 因為如果你等待你會得到兩個 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了現代醫學 , 我加入了一份專注在過去的76歲 , 我比以前更有生產力 , 而且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率 , 結合青少年的健康 , 治癒精神病患的治療方式 , 讓奇蹟轉變為永續性和保育 , 減少有50%的身體復活率 , 改變自殺恐怖攻擊 , 讓家庭的恐怖攻擊 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說:許多生命的謎題 , 可以透過了解你的時間觀點和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這點子很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	今日的頭條數有多少 ? 一百年 ? 一百年 ? kirkcron的 「 長新聞 」 計畫 , 不僅僅是現今的重要故事 , 數十年來 , 甚至數十年來 , 在ted2010年來 , 他對我們的未來有著高光亮的頭條 ,
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球性的議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、科學、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞是真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞上淹沒了 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單單單單單單發出三千五千萬個新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在漫長的過程中有多少故事會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個很長的基金會計畫 , 是由tedtster所創立的 , 包括kevinkel和stewart品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們正在尋找的新聞故事 , 可能是現在的50到100 , 000年 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你看過那些過濾器的新聞時 , 很多來自路線 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 要從a.p 。 這會發生在十年內嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	在50或100年內 , 這會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好 , 這有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年 , 最重要的故事是經濟 , 我很快地打賭 , 不久後 , 這個特定的衰退將會是古老的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事對未來會有不同呢 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 讓我們來看看科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會透過我們的血液修復 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	某天就已經存在了 , 如果你是老鼠 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的故事:nanobees把腫瘤放到真正的甲蟲裡 , 它們會把基因送到大腦裡 ; 一個他們建造的機器人 , 可以穿過人類身體 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那麼資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今我們有難以養育六十億人 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	昨天我們聽到的 , 有超過十億人飢餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國會沒有基因改造的作物 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲有十億的研究 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會很不一樣 , 如果中國設立了安德拉 , 他們就有可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經克服了美國最大的汽車市場 , 他們把德國超越了 , 成為最大的出口 , 他們開始在孩子身上做dna測試 , 選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方式來推回我們所知的限制 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷有一隻螞蟻 , 現在已經傳播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一種自主的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了 , 科學不再需要我們 , 生命也不需要我們 ; 生命也不需要我們 ; 一萬二十萬年後的微生物爆發 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 沒有我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但過去一年 , 我的選項是這個:在月球上找到的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓它變得更容易把蟻群放到那裡 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能 , 或在這個房間裡的人可能會寫一個大的檢查 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:在漫長的跑步中 , 有些新聞比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡林普林科展出來自卡斯坦航行到土星 , 專注於它最大的月球 , 泰坦 , 在弗雷德拉德 , 似乎是拍攝冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、空間、科技、宇宙、視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡林林彼得•米科佛羅我們要滿足我們 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的十八分鐘 , 我要帶你們到一個旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是你和我過去幾年的旅程 , 大約五十年前 , 人類第一次站在地球上 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那五十年裡 , 我們不僅僅是在月球上 , 我們已經把機械太空船放到所有星球上 , 我們還在小行星上 , 我們已經和彗星共存了 , 在這個時候 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 在這個時機上 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 身為一個行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人任務都是更大的人類旅程之一:旅程 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 了解我們的起源 , 了解地球 , 我們的地球 , 我們的地球 , 來到這裡 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 我們可能去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 在1980年代初 , 我們一直在坐著土星 , 但土星的調查已經變得更獨立 , 遠遠超過七年 , 在2004年夏天的太空船旅行中 , 在2004年夏天的夏天 , 到達西尼西尼太空飛行 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是富有的星球系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 顯然地分析 , 和這個系統的調查有巨大的宇宙 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單單單單研究ring , 我們就學了很多星系和氣體 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是一幅美麗的安德魯•阿拉•阿拉 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是一塊美麗的翅膀星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝的 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是真正的一部分 , 也是一個更大的人類旅程 , 來了解周圍的所有事物的連結 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們我們 , 卡西尼所學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看我們過去兩年半的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把兩個最令人興奮的故事集中在這個重大的探險探險探險發展中 , 我們在土星周圍進行 , 過去的兩年半 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是由一個非常大且多樣化的月球組成的 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	他們從幾公里的尺寸到美國的大小 , 大到比例大於美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們所拍攝的最美麗的照片 , 事實上 , 用一些月球來呈現土星 。 這裡是石頭的土星 , 接著 , 這是土星展示了ringgeon的邊緣 , 讓你們看出它們的垂直薄 , 用月亮的土星 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星的四十七顆月球是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是泰坦和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的月球 , 直到卡斯坦到達那裡 , 我們在太陽系中仍有最大的延伸 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這是個很長的身體 , 很感興趣的人 , 看了行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有非常大、厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為是我們在地球上所擁有的環境 , 或者至少在過去 , 比太陽系中的任何其他身體都一樣 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣大部分都是分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸的 , 除了它的大氣層被簡單的有機材料困惑 , 像是甲烷和東方 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在泰坦大氣層中升高 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 組成零粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種棲息無所不在 , 完全是全球和鼓舞道德 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用眼睛看不到表面 , 看不見光譜的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些零粒子 , 在我們接觸到卡西尼之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫柔地向地表 , 以厚度有機的地表 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	像同等 , 泰坦和石油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和eane , 可能是泰坦的表面溫度 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是把水放在地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣層中 , 它是可容忍的 , 因此 , 意識到這個環境會帶到整個奇怪的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在雲層上 , 上面有數百公里的夏季 , 預防任何陽光從表面到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是1.0度的350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管寒冷 , 你可以在泰坦的表面下降雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在地球上 , 雨水的做法是:它會形成河流和洞穴 ; 它可以創造出峽谷 ; 它可以在大型蝙蝠和螃蟹中池塘 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以洗掉高山峰和山丘 , 到低地 , 停止思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 泰坦的高音是黑暗的 , 像地球上的深海線一樣深 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	很冷 , 它是eerie , 它很糟糕 , 可能是雨水 , 你可能站在湖邊 , 米克萊根的陰影中 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在加入卡斯坦的表面前的景象 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在泰坦發現了什麼 , 雖然它在細節裡 , 不像這個故事一樣令人驚訝 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼人一樣 , 像一個叢林冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如同我所說的 , 它有著厚厚的大氣 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是聖聖聖的背景 , 由太陽的背景 , 帶著光環當作美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪個 。 這是個非常強烈的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼有樂器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的相機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮和黑色區域 , 這和我們之間的距離差不多 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這太神秘了:我們無法找出我們在泰坦看到的東西 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域時 , 你會開始看到一些我們不知道的東西 。 你看到一些圓圈 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石 , 但在泰坦的表面有非常少的隕石 , 意思是 , 這是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來是昆蟲 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來就像是分離的 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線條 , 它就表示有碎片 , 就像一個錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但 , 我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到在我們進入軌道的六個月之後 , 一個事件發生了許多人被視為卡斯坦的高速調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是熱氣探測器的部署 , 歐洲的熱氣管探測器 , 卡斯坦在太陽系的七年間 , 我們將它帶到泰坦的大氣層 , 花了兩半小時的時間 , 降落在表面上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只是想強調這個事件的重要性 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外星太陽系上登陸了人類史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我腦海中 , 這場事件應該是和美國各地的各個城市各地的標誌遊行 , 很遺憾的是 , 這不是如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	原因是另一個原因 。 這是國際任務 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國 , 慶祝慶祝慶祝 , 慶祝文章在英語中 , 美國人 , 德國、法國和義大利人和義大利人 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個移動的示範: 「 聯合國 」 應該要說的 「 聯合國 」 和 「 真正的國家 」 結合在一起 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 它是個很大的難以探索一個星球系統 , 為了了解所有人類歷史 , 人類一直不可思議 , 現在人類真的碰到它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我的意思是 , 我剛剛剛談到它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	這是個很有情感的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 而且你也不應該 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但 , 總之 , 探測到大氣層的測量 , 同時也採用了純淨的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 史丹的第一張圖片是怎麼樣的 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那是個令人震驚的事 , 因為我們想要那些從軌道上拍的照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個不公平的模式 , 一個地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這是一種延伸的乾淨模式 , 只由液體的流動而形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以遵循這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們如何轉換 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這個頻道轉換成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你正在看著海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一些海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是16公里 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是8公里拍攝的照片 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好吧 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 這大概是航空的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要在美國飛機旅行 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	所以 , 這是你在泰坦航空的窗戶 , 當你飛過泰坦的表面時 , 你會看到這張照片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器回到表面 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 先生先生 , 第一張從外太陽系中拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水泡 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	顯然 , 它在其中一個平面 , 黑色區域 , 沒有洞察覺 。 所以這不是我們登陸的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	裡面的探測器基本上是泥土平等的 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一種不穩定的地面 , 被液態甲烷困在地上 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	這可能是這樣 , 這個材料被我們看到的高地洗掉 , 花了數十億年的時間 , 降低低地下降 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是飢餓探測器的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然沒有標誌在我們的影像中 , 甚至在熱帶的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 我們發現了沙丘 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好的 , 這是我們在泰坦的平等區域的電影 , 展示這些塵埃 。 這些是100公尺高 , 由幾公里 , 分開 , 以幾公里和哩 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百個 , 到一千或一百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是沙漠沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到塵埃 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 很驚訝的是 , 沒有液體 , 直到終於 , 我們看到北極地區湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在南極的南極區域 , 有一場湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大概是拉克斯塔里約的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 只有一週半前 , 我們飛過了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們在卡普利亞海的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎是液體 , 我們不了解的原因 , 或至少這個季節 , 都很顯然是泰坦的極端 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我認為你會同意 , 我們發現泰坦是很棒的 , 神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但很奇怪 , 但很奇怪的是地球的形式 , 和地理的多樣性 , 以及一個巨大的地理多樣化的世界 , 只是在太陽系中對複雜和豐富的世界 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們去了土衛二 , 土衛二是一顆小月球 , 大約是泰坦的10大小 。 你可以在英格蘭旁邊看到它 , 讓你們看到大小 , 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白色的 , 它的表面很明顯是碎形的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二的母親被發現在南極 , 我們看到南極的南極 , 我們發現了這個脆弱的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組合 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	這些碎片是由有機材料組成 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個地區 , 南極地區 , 已經進化了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就像是發現地球上的南極比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們採取更多的圖片 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片的噴射噴射 , 將數百英里延伸到太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像拿出來時 , 我們看到這些珠子餵飽了粉紅色 , 事實上 , 在其他的影像中 , 數千英里的太空 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊和研究像這樣的影像 , 像這樣 , 就像這張照片 , 想著來自卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們在結論中得到的結論 , 這些噴泉可能是從土衛二表面下的液態水排放出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有了 , 液態水、有機物質和熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能在現代行星探索的聖道上 , 或換句話說 , 一個可能適合生存生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在太陽系中其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因發生了不一次 , 但在我們的太陽系中 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 只有兩倍 , 那就表示 , 這意味著 , 整個宇宙中發生了驚人的數量 , 且它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是唯一的行星 , 我們所知道的就是生活 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨特的 , 到目前為止 , 我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	假如在1960年代 , 在座任何人都很高興 , 我們都認同你 , 如果你沒有 , 好 , 你會記得在阿波羅88號太空人拍的這張很有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是地球第一次被太空影像影像 , 它對宇宙的感受有著巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼先拍了一幅相同的照片 , 沒有人眼前看到的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的一面 , 從土星的另一邊看到的 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可思議的圖片中 , 你看到太陽的主要節奏 , 你看到太陽的反射影像 , 你看到這張圖 , 事實上 , 是由土衛二的爆發 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠棒 , 我們就可以在這個美麗的星球上 , 看我們自己的星球 , 撞上了土星的手臂 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些很深的移動 , 讓自己從afar , 捕捉我們的小小、藍色的星球 , 在其他世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從這方面得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從一半年前從這個發現的旅程中得到最好的獎勵 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人在災難後 , 愛滋病的消失後 , 隱藏了未被忽視的土地和未知的道路 。 在短短的演講中 , 谷歌的卡拉多•卡達•卡德加德瓦德•德薩德的地圖 , 一群人在全球地圖上繪製的地圖工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近 , 卡拉格達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cycclonenagis破壞了manmar 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要打破人民和供應地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有幫助到網路受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 世界上只有15%被繪製到地理細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國的頭條 , 到世界上大部分的大面孔:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但幫忙來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40名志工用了新的軟體來繪製一萬二十萬公里的路徑 , 三千個醫院、邏輯和信仰點 。
and it took them four days .	花了四天 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體嗎 ? google地圖製造者 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖標記者是科技 , 我們每個人都能在當地地圖地圖地圖地圖地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從路到河 , 從學校到當地企業 , 影片儲存到角落店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾•帕爾•德魯多德明白了 , 對於大部分開發中國家的經濟利潤的關鍵 , 是要擊敗大量的未預算的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 一兆美金在印度的土地保持無前例 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 一百七十個國家有數百萬個使用者 , 創造出一種細節的地圖 , 從來沒有想過 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	每處都有熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看一些使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 人們在這個170個國家繪製世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑 , 只是在塞內加爾購買一條路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	更靠近家 , 查羅拉 , 一個n.g.g.路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算數位的結果 , 特徵辨識 , 機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個邀請給我們未受歡迎的星球70% 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落了十個月的非暴力抗議 , 阻止他們橄欖球 。 你聽見了嗎 ? 巴西的電影電影朱利亞•朱利亞•朱利亞•朱利亞 , 問我們為什麼只有專注在以色列的衝突中 , 而不是在非暴力的領導人 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情心、娛樂、電影、和平、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱利亞:注意到非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我一直投入我的人生 , 記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的方式結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 我花了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 從以色列士兵和居住者身上 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖忘記一個龐大的國家非暴力運動 , 終止職業 , 並在地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在這地面和感知之間的分歧是為什麼我們還沒有巴勒斯坦和平的重要原因之一
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來這裡談的是注意力、注意力的力量 , 以及在西岸的非暴力運動和發展 , 加薩和其他地方 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大部分的非暴力 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採取非暴力 , 而是讓我們開始關注那些已有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明這一點 , 藉由帶你到這個叫做budrus的村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個區隔障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙會被建造在村莊上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 被圍繞 , 所以他們會失去免費取得西岸的其他地方 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發當地的領導 , 他們發射了和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種情況 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的影片 , 所以你對地面的看法是有意義的 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦婦女:我們被告知 , 從以色列 , 會分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯這裡 , 我們意識到牆壁會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:這句話其實 , 創造出一個錯誤的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你邀請一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你參與了幾十位以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的行動主義者:沒有比非暴力反對更害怕的軍隊 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有人能這麼做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩可以這麼做 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔利黨員:我們必須擁抱傳統思維的思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈瑪•派派派對:我們是完全駭客 , 我們想要把它傳播給所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	查理:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬和流行的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞編輯器:船長持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列的邊境警察被寄給群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活躍的 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是泰迪 。 拍攝到任何地方 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列的行動主義者:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊還有其他的 , 甚至還沒有編寫 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會停止 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	主持人:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	查理:我們可以做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴拉:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事 , 我驚訝的是 , 國際媒體失敗了 , 七年前發生了非凡的事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布德魯斯成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過10個月的和平抗拒之後 , 說服以色列政府 , 搬離土地和綠色線 , 國際化的界限在以色列和巴勒斯坦地區 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布魯德斯的抗藥性從西岸傳播到西岸和巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然留在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默的後果對非暴力的可能性有著深刻的後果 , 或甚至在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒和非暴力抗拒 , 分享一個非常重要的事 ; 他們都是劇院尋求觀眾的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一常被前面的封面 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 對於非暴力領袖來說 , 很難讓公民歧視的社區變成一種可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能不會對房間的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	為了讓孩子們越來越大的抗議方式 , 就是給他注意他第一次丟上手指 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	螞蟻會變成童年心理學家稱之為功能行為的行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能激勵或獨立的行為 , 只要給予孩子或關注 。
but that's true for adults too .	但 , 對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能受到影響 , 依據國際社群選擇專注注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東的衝突的核心 , 將和平帶給我們 , 將非暴力的行為轉變成一個功能的行為 , 藉由給予現今的非暴力領袖的注意力 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在西銀行、加薩和東耶路撒冷的過程中 , 我看到了即使一部紀錄片可以影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做壁畫的村莊 , 位於耶路撒冷 , 社區面臨了非常相似的折磨 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞 , 失去許多土地 , 卻沒有自由 , 不論是西岸銀行或猶太人 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們花了大約兩年的時間使用非暴力 , 但從沒有人專注的注意力開始成長 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們把最好的位置和獨立的展示給約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織員說 , 村民們 , 在電影中看到布德魯斯的故事 , 感受到 , 有人追隨他們所做的事 , 人們關心 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列的邊緣 , 有一種新的和平運動叫做義大利亞特 , 這意味著希伯特的固定性 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者被當作是他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告 , 以色列之前從來沒有活躍 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	牆壁和固態運動的例子 , 顯示 , 即使是一個小型的獨立電影 , 可以在改變非暴力行為的行為中扮演一個角色 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家的力量 , 如果他們開始覆蓋週末非暴力的示範 , 例如bilin , ni , ni , 華納 , 華納 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像siikharharh , 絲瓦爾 , 那些非暴力領袖就會變得更糟糕、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像他們從未發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但 , 我第一次看到如果我們這麼做 , 他們就會乘以倍數 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們乘以多 , 他們的影響會在以色列人的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力是終於能解開這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明 , 像布德魯這樣的地方是非暴力的 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給他們注意力 , 這樣他們就可以證明它在各地運作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙斯汀克有一個簡單且強大的領導模式 , 都從黃金圈開始 , 提出問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德•金 , 以及威脅兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	布洛伊、商業、企業家、領導人、銷售、銷售、成功、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙斯汀克:領導者有多偉大的啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不當我們假設的時候 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好的 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能得到這些假設的成就時 , 會怎麼解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 一年後 , 畢竟 , 他們比所有競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才華 , 同一個機構 , 同一個顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們看起來有點不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德王引領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是唯一的偉大主持人 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何 , 威脅兄弟們能夠想出控制 , 權力的飛行 , 當其他團隊有更好的資金時 , 更好的資金 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成男人飛行 , 威脅兄弟打擊了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我的觀點 , 改變了我的想法如何運作 , 它甚至深深地改變了我在運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大且鼓舞領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果或馬丁•路德國 , 或他們都認為 , 行為和溝通的方式都一樣 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	對其他人來說 , 完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是複製它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠啟發別人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不管你稱它為你不同的價值建議或你的正義過程或你的使用 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但 , 非常少人或組織都知道他們為何做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	「 為何 」 我不代表 「 做利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	結果是 , 結果總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	根據 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上你會離開床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們認為 , 我們採取行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式來自外面 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清楚的事物到謎題 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但靈感的領袖和靈感的組織 , 不管他們的大小 , 不管他們的產業都認為 , 行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都得到 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 一個行銷訊息可能聽起來就像這樣: 「 我們製造了很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮地設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷是這樣做 , 那就是大部分銷售的成果 , 那就是我們大多數人交流的交流 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說 , 我們怎麼做 , 我們說我們是不同的 , 或我們如何做得更好 , 我們期待某種行為 , 一個投票 , 像這樣 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做事 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體 , 它有雷射座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果的溝通方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信在挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思維 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓產品美麗的設計 , 簡單地使用和使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛剛剛剛剛製作了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同了嗎 ? 你準備好要從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是逆轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	對我們來說 , 人們不買你做的事 ; 人們買你為何做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都非常舒服 , 從蘋果買電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但是我們也很舒服地買蘋果或蘋果的手機 , 或是蘋果的dvr , 或是蘋果的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但正如我之前所說的 , 蘋果公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西會從任何競爭者中分散 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格來製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 蓋茲公路出現了平面螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格來製造平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	數年來 , 他們一直在製造平面螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾出發了3個玩家和pdas , 他們製作了很大的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的產品 , 沒有人買了 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像 , 買一名mp3的玩家 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買一個mp3的玩家 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標是不要和任何需要你所擁有的商業 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人商業 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	這是最好的部分:我告訴你們的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	它全都在生物學的條件上 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你仔細看人類大腦的交叉 , 從頂端看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦實際上被破壞成三種主要元素 , 完全與黃金圈相互聯繫 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的同性腦 , 我們的新皮質 , 和 「 什麼 」 的層次對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質對我們的理性和分析和語言負責 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個區塊組成了肢體的大腦 , 我們的肢體大腦負責我們所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人的行為 , 所有決策 , 也沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是沒有驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通時 , 我們會直接到大腦控制行為的一部分 , 然後我們允許人們用我們所說的最好東西和做些什麼 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的地方 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道嗎 , 有時候你能給別人所有事實和數字 , 他們說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節的說法 , 但這不是對的 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會使用這個版本 , 不是 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好的目標是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或有時候你會說你正帶著你的心臟 , 或是你帶著你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破它 , 這些不是其他的身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你肢體的大腦中 , 控制決策的一部分 , 而不是語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為何你做的事 , 人們會回應你為何做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或更重要的是 , 更重要的是 , 要成為你所做的事 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣地 , 目標不只是要賣給你需要什麼的人 ; 目標是要賣給你相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是僱用你相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們 , 因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用你相信的人 , 他們會為你所相信的 , 他們會為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	別的是 , 這裡有更好的例子 , 比有威脅兄弟更好 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部份人都不知道samuelpierproley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀早期 , 權力的男人飛行的追求就像一天的點 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelperponley , 我們假設 , 成為成功的回應 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的觀點 , 同樣的三件事:受試者、錯誤的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	它總是相同的三件事 , 所以我們來探究它 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelperprley被戰爭部門給予五萬美金 , 來找出飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛大學 , 工作在加密森氏症上 , 非常有關聯性 ; 他知道每天所有的大思維 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用最好的心智 , 可以找到和市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他周圍 , 每個人都在追蹤拉利 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierproley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠離俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾 , 威爾•威爾 , 他們沒有我們所認為的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們在他們的自行車店上付出的夢想 ; 不是單一的兄弟團隊的團隊有大學教育 , 甚至是ville或wilbur ; 紐約時報跟著他們走過來 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別是 , 奧維爾爾和沃爾堡是由一個目標所驅動的 , 由一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelparngley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他的追求是富裕的 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	再來看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信聰明的兄弟夢想的人 , 和他們一起合作 , 用血液、汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說故事 , 每次威脅兄弟走出去 , 他們就必須花五組的部分 , 因為那是他們會在上班前爬多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在1903年12月17日 , 威脅兄弟們飛行 , 沒有人會在那裡 , 甚至沒有人會經歷它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了它 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 拉利的動機是錯誤的:白天的兄弟飛行 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是很棒的發現 , 傢伙 , 我會改善你的科技 , 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是首先 , 他沒有富有 , 他沒有有名 , 所以他辭掉了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引你相信的那些人很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做創新的法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你肯定知道這個詞 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們的第一個2%和1%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	下一個百分之十三十五的人口是早期的選民 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期 , 你的主要 , 你的主要和你的缺陷 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到觸控電話的唯一理由是 , 因為你再也不能再買羅字手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個大規模的各個地方 , 但創新的法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大規模成功或大規模的預算 , 你就無法達到這個點子 , 直到你達到15%和18%的市場拘留點 , 然後系統的限制 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你在新生意上有什麼轉換 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你們: 「 喔 , 這大概是10% 。 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試試超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有百分之十的 「 得到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就好像那種腸子感覺: 「 喔 , 他們只是得到 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到你在做生意之前的樣子 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這一小塊你必須靠近的 , 就像傑夫摩爾稱它為 「 跨越椅子 」 , 因為 , 早期大部分的人都不會嘗試 , 直到他人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新家和早期的選舉者 , 他們很舒服地做出那些罪惡的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒服地做出這些直覺的決策 , 由他們對世界的相信而驅動的決定 , 不僅僅是產品能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在線上六個小時去買iphone , 當他們第一次出門時 , 當你可以走進房間時 , 買了一部衣服 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕上花了四萬美金 , 儘管科技是郊區 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為科技太棒了 , 他們為自己做這件事 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一位 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 , 你做的就是證明你相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	一個人在第一小時買iphone的原因 , 站在六個小時之內 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們希望每個人看他們:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及有名的成功成功的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 成功的回應是金錢和正確的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從約八或九年前到目前為止 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手上沒有缺陷 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受歡迎 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我一直都在我垃圾時期的dvr上投票 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一種商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約30或40美金 , 然後放大了 , 它從來沒有交易到10 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至在6 , 除了幾隻小骨頭 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為 , 當tivo發射了他們的產品 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一產品 , 暫停電視、技能商業、重新設計電視 , 並且記住你的觀點習慣 , 不用問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	歷史上大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	假如他們說: 「 如果你是想要控制你人生的每一個方面的人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停住電視、技能商業化 , 將你的觀點習慣、等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為何做 , 而你做的事就是你所相信的證據 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的解放法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 25萬人在華盛頓博士說話 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有邀請 , 而且沒有網站來檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	你該怎麼做 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一的男人 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受苦的美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走過來告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	那些相信他所相信的原因的人 , 他們會自己做自己 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人發聲 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	洛杉磯 , 25萬人在右日出現在對的時間 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他發表 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己發表 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在公車上旅行八小時 , 站在華盛頓的華盛頓區 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 而不是黑色的白人:百分之25的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世界上有兩種法律:那些由較高的權威所組成的人 , 那些是由男人所組成的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到人類所做出的所有法律 , 不管我們在一個更高的權威中所做出的法律 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好發生了 , 民權運動是幫助他帶來生命的完美 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們遵循 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物 , 用他們的12point計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 還有那些領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些引領我們激勵我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們遵守那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們遵循那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為何 」 開始的 「 開始 」 的人有能力啟發他們周圍的人或找到其他激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你在正確的方向下移動 ? 神經學家neil負責研究周圍的神經機制 , 以及他們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neil燃燒:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡在哪裡 ?
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在一個大停車場時 , 我們要如何記得我們在哪裡停車 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這裡有個問題在家 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們從海馬迴開始 , 黃色顯示 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損害 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記住 , 包含你停車在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	在拉丁文為 「 海底 」 之後 , 它是相反的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像其他的大腦 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦大約有一百億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元互相溝通 , 藉由發送小脈衝或訊號接觸到彼此 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體形成了兩個細胞 , 非常密集的連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 藉由從老鼠或老鼠身上記錄下來 , 或探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	我們將想像一下 , 我們在這個老鼠的海馬體錄下的單一神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一小塊電力時 , 就會有一個紅點 , 點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們所看到的是 , 這種神經元知道每當老鼠在環境中流入一個特定的地方 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會訊號傳送到大腦的其他部分 , 藉由發送一個小的電訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元的功能視為動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物在其環境中的不同部分時 , 牠們會發出不同的神經元 , 就像在這個方形盒子裡顯示的 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們共同組成了大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	地方細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了一個電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	放置在他們的海馬桶裡的細胞會發動 , 變成活躍 , 開始發送電脈衝 , 每當他們穿過某個特定的區域時 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個地方細胞怎麼知道哪裡的老鼠或人在環境中 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞顯示 , 環境的界線是很重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 最頂端的一個 , 例如要開火 , 會在他們老鼠的牆壁之間 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展盒子時 , 旋轉就會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的一個位置 , 每當有一面牆靠近南方 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放另一壁牆 , 那麼細胞會在兩個地方火 , 不管在南方有牆 , 都是動物在盒子裡探索的 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測 , 使你周遭的界限和方向的距離和方向 , 尤其是海馬體的重要性 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 細胞被發現為海馬體 , 它的反應是直接偵測到界線 , 或邊緣 , 以特定的距離 , 或滑鼠來探索 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物接近牆壁或邊緣 , 不管是邊緣或邊緣的牆 , 或圓形的牆壁 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物在四處跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發射 , 每當南部有一塊圓形 , 不管是桌子或牆壁的邊緣 , 或甚至兩座桌子之間的差距 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	因此 , 我們認為 , 細胞會決定動物在哪裡去探索 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體的位置 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或是你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們能讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常他們都很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們和地方細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個案例中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小方形的環境中 , 如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你把環境變得更大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被壓倒了 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你記得旗幟在哪裡儲存在你所有地方的細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回溯到這個位置的位置 , 這樣你就可以最好的配合你所在的區域細胞的現狀模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那引導你回到你想記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在移動何處 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些外在的路徑 , 或許我們停下來 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們的動作 , 我們能把這個路線整合起來 , 幾乎是頭部的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	放置細胞也得到這種條件 , 從一種叫做網格細胞的輸入 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞再次發現 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 它們有點像放置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠在各處探索時 , 每個個體都在一整條不同的地點 , 在整個環境中 , 都在一個很普通的三角形圖 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾張圖片中記錄下來 , 在不同的顏色中 , 每個顏色都有相似的圖案 , 每個細胞的圖形 , 就會轉換到其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的一顆火在這張圖上 , 綠色的那張 , 和這張照片上的藍色 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起來 , 就好像老鼠可以把虛擬的地圖放到它的環境中 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的拉丁和長期的線條 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就能用自己的動作 , 才能知道它在環境中是什麼 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有圖像的圖案都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的相同位置 , 以橘色的角度來看 , 意思是 , 大腦的所有網格活動應該改變 , 根據這六個方向 , 或在六個方向進行的方向 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放在磁共振儀裡 , 讓他們做一些小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我展示給你看的 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人體皮質上看到它 , 這是你在老鼠身上看到的同一部分 。
so back to homer .	回到家裡 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他車子的距離和方向的位置 , 要在他停車的位置中展開和界限 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這會被無限的細胞所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車公園中拿出來的路徑 , 它會被代表在網格細胞中 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓地方細胞消防 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回溯到他移動的地點 , 這樣才能找到最好的圖案 , 正是他腦中的位置細胞的位置 , 正是他停車車的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那位視覺特徵 , 像是他的車子是否在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被浪費了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 ,
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這張圖案 , 我們在一系列的位置中看到 , 在我們做各種自動化記憶任務時 , 例如 , 記得你最後一次去婚禮 , 例如 , 舉例來說 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能就是我們周遭空間的神經機制 , 同時也用來產生視覺圖像 , 這樣我們就能重建空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想想像它們時 , 我們會發生的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從一個地方細胞一起啟動彼此 , 維持這些密度的連結 , 然後反應界線的細胞 , 來創造你的觀點的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種細胞 , 頭部的方向部細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 他們會像同情的同情 , 例如你所面對的哪種方式 。
